=500  \\$aThe Katharineum in Lübeck was a gymnasium famous for its curriculum of the trivium (grammar, rhetoric and logic), the quadrivium (arithmetic, geometry, music, and astronomy), as well as the study of literature, poetry, drama, philosophy, history, art, and languages.

=500  \\$a Yearbook of the Katharineum in Lübeck, a gymnasium famous for its curriculum of the trivium (grammar, rhetoric and logic), the quadrivium (arithmetic, geometry, music, and astronomy), as well as the study of literature, poetry, drama, philosophy, history, art, and languages.

=500  \\$aChristian Reuter was a German historian and pedagogue and director of the Katharineum in Lübeck 1904-1915. 
=500  \\$aLecture on the history of the gymnasium in separate volume (26E18p)

=100  \\$aHannetaire, Jean-Nicolas d'$d1718-1780$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3010923$98332
=245  \\$aObservations sur l'art du comédien, et sur d'autres objets concernant cette profession en général
=250  \\$aRev. ed.
=260  \\$bSociété Typographique$c1774
=300  \\$axvi-348-[2] pages
=500  \\$aBookseller's slip: "In-8 e xvi, 348,& [1] non ch., relié plein veau blond, dos à nerfs orné (rel d'époque). Fils d'un peintre de renom, c'est le seul écrit de cet acteur fortuné qui fit carrière en Allemagne, en Belgique (où il fut directeur du Théâtre de la Monnaie), et en France. Rédigé à l'usage des prétendants acteurs et actrices, il contient de nombreux détails sur la vie des troupes, le jeu d'acteur et le status de comédien. Statut fort peu en odeur de sainteté, l'église excommuniant alors la profession. D'Hannetaire « en vertu d'un ancien usage de la comédie » renonça en 1768 par-devant notaire au status, mais pas à la pratique. Légères épidermures sans gravité, infime rousseur encadrant le titre, bon exemplaire."

=590  \\$aAbgebildet an dem unverendertem Vorsatz des frommen Patriarchen Jacobs, als er bey schwerem Dienste, seine ihm versprochene, hertzgewüntschte Jungfraw Rahel, nicht allein vierzehen gantzer Jahr vor dem Ehelichen Beylager, sondern auch bestendiglichen geliebet und lieb gehalten, biß in den Todt, und nach dem Tode: oder die wunderschöne Historia und denckwürdige Geschicht, der Heyrat Jacobs, im ersten Buch Mosis am 29. Capittel. Zu sonderbarem unvergessenem Ruhm, und stetwehrendem Gedächtnüß auch hochnützlichen Erinnerungen, denen Ehrenvesten, Wolbenambten, Erbarn und vorsichtigen jungen Gesellen, allen und jeden, Bürgers Söhnen, und Zuchtliebenden Jünglingen, so wol allen und jeden, züchtigen, Edlen, viel Ehrentugentreichen Jungfrawen, Bürgers Töchtern, hoch und nider Standes Personen, in der Uhralten, mächtigen, und Edlen Provinz, des Christlichen Landes Preussen, sonderlich der drey See-Haupt- und Handelsstädte, Dantzig, Thoren, und Margenberg, in gebührender Unterthänigkeit, mit erzehlung der aller denckwürdigsten, und lustigsten Historien, dedicirt: durch Abrahamum Hossmannum, Laubanensum Lusatium, Sacr. Cæsar. Majestat. Historicum.

=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aLackington, James$d1746-1815$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q6137696$98413
=245  \\$aMemoirs of the Forty-Five First Years of the Life of James Lackington, Bookseller
=250  \\$a10th ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bLackington$c1795
=300  \\$a328 pages
=500  \\$aJames Lackington (1746-1815) was a bookseller who is credited with revolutionizing the British book trade.  He is best known for refusing credit at his shop which allowed him to reduce the price of books throughout his store. He printed catalogues of his stock; according to Lackington's biography, the first edition contained 12,000 titles. He bought whole libraries and published writers' manuscripts. He also saved remaindered books from destruction and resold them at bargain prices, firmly believing that books were the key to knowledge, reason and happiness and that everyone, no matter their economic background, social class or gender, had the right to access books at cheap prices. (source: wiki)

=100  \\$aDesforges, Pierre-Jean-Baptiste Choudard dit$d1746-1806$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3024390$97425
=245  \\$aMémoires anecdotes pour servir a l'histoire de M. Duliz
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bHarding$c1739
=300  \\$a206 pages$bfrontispiece in red and black ink
=500  \\$aMarie Pélissier (1706-1749) was a French operatic soprano. At the Paris Opera in 1722, she began her career, which was noted for her artistic skill and a scandal, until her retirement in 1741. A scandal involving the theft of gold and money from the Jewish financier François Lopez Dulis, led to Pélissier's dismissal on February 15, 1734, whereupon she fled to London. She was back at the Paris Opera on April 19, 1735, remaining there until retiring in October 1741.

=100  \\$aLobwasser, Ambrosius$d1515-1585$4trl$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q73956$95226
=245  \\$aPsalmen Davids
=260  \\$aBernburg$bGerhard$c1728
=300  \\$a[xiv]-406-[10] pages
=500  \\$aAmbrosius Lobwasser (1515–1585) was a German humanist and translator, born in Saxony. He is best known for his Psalter des Königlichen Propheten David, published in 1573 (Leipzig). This metrical psalter, a translation of the Genevan Psalter, became one of the standard psalm-books used by the evangelical churches of the German-speaking lands, including Switzerland (the Genevan Psalter had been written in French). The Lobwasser psalter was widely reprinted into the 1800s.

In allen Gemeinden dero Landen einzuführen und zu gebrauchen

=041  \\$aita$hlat
=100  \\$aFigliucci, Felice$dc. 1524-c. 1590$4trl$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3742149$98465
=245  \\$aCatechismo cioè Istruttione secondo il Decreto del Concilio di Trento a' Parochi
=260  \\$aVenice$bAngelieri$c1605
=300  \\$a[xv]-578-[20] pages
=500  \\$aCatechism of the Catholic Counter-Reformation with the norms and conclusions laid down by the Council of Trent (closed in 1563) in response to the Lutheran Reformation.
=500  \\$aPope Pius IV entrusted the composition of the Catechism to four distinguished theologians: Leonardo Marini, Archbishop of Lanciano; Muzio Calini, Archbishop of Zara; Egidio Foscherari, Bishop of Modena; and Francisco Foreiro, a Portuguese Dominican.
Three cardinals were appointed to supervise the work. Charles Borromeo superintended the redaction of the original Italian text, which was finished in 1564. Cardinal William Sirletus then gave it the final touches, and the famous Humanists, Julius Pogianus and Paulus Manutius, translated it into classical Latin.
=500  \\$aFelice Figliucci (Felix Filliucius, cloister name Alexus) (c. 1525 – c. 1590), an Italian humanist, philosopher, and theologian translated the Latin Catechism back into Italian in 1567 at the order of the Pope. 
=534  \\$cCatechismus ex decreto Concilii Tridentini ad parochos Pii V jussu editus, Romae (Rome: Manuzio, 1566)
=648  \0$a16th Century (1501-1600)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7017$920944
=648  \0$a17th Century (1601-1700)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7016$920923

He was a collaborator of the «Giornale dei Letterati d'Italia», member of the Academy of Arcadia and of that of Crusca from 1727. Besides promoting literary initiatives, he was a bibliophile and book collector.
=500  \\$aFrancesco Scipione Maffei (1675-1755) was a Venetian writer and art critic, author of many articles and plays. Maffei was of the illustrious family that originated in Bologna. He studied for five years in Parma, at the Jesuit College, and afterwards, from 1698, at Rome, where he became a member of the Accademia degli Arcadi. He then founded an "Arcadian Academy" in his hometown Verona. In 1709, he went to Padua, where he briefly collaborated with Apostolo Zeno and Antonio Valisnieri in editing the ambitious literary periodical the Giornale de' Letterati d'Italia, which had but a short career. Subsequently, an acquaintance with the actor Riccoboni led him to exert himself for the improvement of dramatic art in Italy and a revitalized Italian theatre.
=500  \\$aScipione Maffei premiered his tragedy Merope in Verona on June 12, 1713; it quickly became popular throughout Italy and beyond. By agreement with Maffei, Voltaire went on to adapt the play, which was eventually staged in 1743 as Mérope.
=500  \\$aMerope was a Queen of Messenia in Greek mythology, daughter of King Cypselus of Arcadia and wife of Cresphontes, the Heraclid king of Messenia. After the murder of her husband and her two older children by Polyphontes (another Heraclid), Merope was forced to marry the murderer, but she managed to save her youngest son Aepytus, whom she sent secretly to Aetolia. Several years later, when Aepytus grew up, he killed Polyphontes with the collaboration of Merope, and he took revenge for the murder of his relatives and the insult to his mother.

=245  \\$aDe snaaksche Clement Marot op zyn praatstoel verhalende over de driehondert koddige historien en snaakeryen
=260  \\$aCologne$bGaillard
=300  \\$a[ii]-320 pages$b5 plates & 1 folded sheet inserted
=500  \\$aCollection of anecdotes, as if from the mouth of the witty and most shrewd among the court jesters Clement Marot, that was published in the middle of the eighteenth century, probably in Amsterdam. The imprint Jacobus Gaillard in Cologne is a fictitious printer's address.
=500  \\$aClement Marot (1496 – 1544) is known, among other things, for his Psalm rhyming of 1541. He was also the court poet to King Francis I. Shortly after his death, all kinds of existing jokes, farces and anecdotes were written to his name, as was the case with his compatriots François Villon and Rabelais. In the Netherlands it was the poet, innkeeper and actor Jan Zoet who published a collection of anecdotes (translated or not, unknown) in 1655 under the title 'Het leven en bedrijf van Clement Marot', a collection that has been reprinted far into the nineteenth century. However 'De snaaksche Clement Marot' only has Marot's name in common with that work.

=500  \\$aJean-François de La Harpe (1739-1803) was a French playwright, writer and literary critic. He took part in the quarrel between the Gluckists and the Piccinists, an aesthetic controversy that divided the Parisian musical world between 1775 and 1779, where the defenders of French opera (Gluckists) and the supporters of Italian music (Piccinists) were opposing each other. La Harpe was, together with Marmontel and d'Alembert, a proponent of Italian music.
=500  \\$aLa Harpe's Literary Correspondence, addressed to the Grand Duke Paul of Russia, is full of theatrical anecdotes about the actors and plays of his time.

=100  \\$aPinot Duclos, Charles$d1704-1772$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q982034$98370
=245  \\$aHistoire de Madame De Luz;  anecdotte du règne d'Henri IV
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bHondt, de$c1741
=300  \\$a426-22 pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=500  \\$aThrough a vivid portrait of a woman of sovereign innocence, Duclos denounces the hypocrisy of a prudish society. Madame de Luz is a sort of libertine Princess of Cleves, a moralist's novel that is also a praise of femininity.
=504  \\$aMadame de Luz is one of the most beautiful women in the kingdom of Henry IV, virtuous and loyal to her husband. She is secretly in love with the Marquis de Saint-Geran, but tries to forget this passion.

Her husband, the Baron de Luz, is involved in a plot led by the Maréchal de Biron, Governor of Burgundy, to overthrow Henry IV. Arrested, the Baron de Luz is threatened with the death penalty. Convinced of his innocence and determined to free him, Madame de Luz intervenes with one of the judges at the trial, Monsieur de Thurin, a suitor whom she had once spurned. Thurin is ready to clear the Baron's name if she accepts his advances. Madame de Luz resists and then gives in to the blackmail. Her life then turns upside down. She has committed a sin from which she will never recover.

=245  \\$aEssai sur le méchanisme des passions en général
=260  \\$aParis$bLe Prieur$c1751
=300  \\$a[ii]- XXVII-56-[12]-189 pages$bfolded page with engraved plate
=500  \\$aFirst edition of this curious and unusual work, in which the author, physician to the polish King Stanislas (Stanisław I Leszczyński 1677-1766) seeks to study the "influence of the passions" on the development of diseases: this is one of the first treatises on the subject, which was very popular at the end of the 18th and beginning of the 19th centuries. The author deals in particular with the effects of music and analyses the way in which singing and instruments can act on the passions

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$4aut$aMeerten-Schilperoort, Anna Barbara van$d1778-1853$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2138933$923916
=245  \\$aAlmanak voor de jeugd voor 1830
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bBeijerinck$c1830
=300  \\$a[x]-110-[2] pages$billustrations some of them coloured, engraved title page
=500  \\$aAlmanak voor de Jeugd was published 1827 - 1839, Amsterdam, by  G.J.A. Beijerinck. 
=500  \\$aThe Almanak voor de Jeugd contained an annual year calendar with religious holidays, and consists mainly of moralising stories and poems specially written for children
=500  \\$aAnna Barbara Van Meerten-Schilperoort, writer, educator and school teacher, is herself responsible for all the stories and the play and will continue to do so over twenty years. For the little poems, which she loves but does not write herself, she is dependent on the input of others. 
=500  \\$aVan Meerten-Schilperoort published several books on education, advice to women, novels, and other works. In 1821–1835, she was the editor of the paper Penelope. Her school became one of the most notable institutes of education for women in the Netherlands. She spoke for difference feminism, and argued that women should be given a more public role in the service of the state. In 1832 she started philanthropic work for the betterment of the conditions of female prisoners, and in 1841, she founded the charity association Hulpbetoon aan Eerlijke en Vlijtige Armoede, which was the first women's organization in the Netherlands. She has been referred to as the founder of the organized women's rights movement in the Netherlands.

=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1740

=500  \\$a"Mr L'Abbé de Villiers, si connu par son Art de prêcher, & par plusieurs autres Ouvrages, qui ont eu l'aprobation du public" (in Oeuvres de Monsieur de Saint Evremond, I,  p.296)
=500  \\$aDe Villiers wrote many works in the seventeenth century, and many biographies and studies are attributed to him, such as Lettres sur l'oraison des quiétistes or Prière en vers sur l'espérance qu'on doit avoir en Jésus-Christ.He  was the first to suspect that Perrault's tales were not written by Charles Perrault's son, as announced by the publishers, but by the academician himself - or at least at second hand. De Villiers joined the Jesuits on 6 June 1666 and distinguished himself in the careers of teaching and preaching. He took the order of priesthood and exercised the holy ministry. In 1689 he left the Jesuits to join the unreformed Cluny order. A writer and essayist, he composed or printed most of the works that came from his pen. Boileau mentions the Abbé de Villiers in his poetry, and calls him "the Matamore of Cluny", "because he had a bold air and imperious speech". He never put his name to his works.

=500  \\$aHenriette-Julie de Murat was an aristocratic French writer of the late 17th century.
=500  \\$aIn 1697 she published Memoirs of the Countess of M***, a two-volume collection of false "memoirs" which was meant as a response to Charles de Saint-Évremond's 1696 book Memoirs of the Life of Count D*** before his Retirement, which had portrayed women as incapable of virtue and fickle. Murat's book was successful and was even translated into English.

=500  \\$aLe Misant(h)rope was a Dutch journal originally published every monday from May 19th 1711 tot December 26th 1712 . Published in 2 vols. in The Hague by T.Johnson in 1711 and 1712. The magazine was reprinted in 1726 (own revision by Van Effen) in The Hague; 1741 (Lausanne/Geneva) and twice in 1742 (Amsterdam and The Hague).
=500  \\$aJustus van Effen was a Dutch author, who wrote chiefly in French but also made crucial contributions to Dutch literature. A journalist, he imitated The Spectator with the publication of the Dutch-language Hollandsche Spectator. He gained international fame as a writer of French periodicals and a translator from English into French, and he is also recognized as one of the most important Dutch language writers of the 18th century and an influential figure of the Dutch Enlightenment
=500  \\$aOften considered as one of the best essayistic texts from the early Enlightenment.
=500  \\$aFrontispiece vol.1 is an engraved portrait of the author by Pieter Tanjé (1706-1761)  after des Angeles (1716-1761)

=100  \\$aEffen, Justus van$d1684-1735$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2574405$98518
=245  \\$aLa Bagatelle, $bou Discours ironiques$n1-2/2
=250  \\$arev. ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bUytwerf$c1742
=300  \\$a2 vols ([xxvi]-300-[8] + 289-[9] pages)$btitle pages in red and black ink
=490  \\$aOeuvres diverses de Mr. Juste van Effen$v3-4/4
=500  \\$aMoral observations in a satirical tone. Interests: fashion, religion, morals. Authors studied: Addison, Swift, La Bruyère.
=500  \\$aDutch Journal published every thursday and monday between 5 mai 1718 and 13 avril 1719. 
=500  \\$aAlready the author of several journals including the first spectator in French (Le Misanthrope), Justus van Effen attempted to capture the Regency spirit in France with La Bagatelle. Produced as a twice-weekly quarter sheet, La Bagatelle included witty observations on contemporary society, literary controversies, bolder, more subversive reflections on questions of religion, as well as short works of poetry and prose. 
=500  \\$aSince 1718, the publication of the Literary Journal had been delayed by the nonchalance of the bookseller Johnson. For van Effen this meant a considerable loss of money, so he sought some compensation. He launched La Bagatelle for personal reasons.
=500  \\$aThe author intended (cf. Preface) to lead men from the ridiculousness of custom and fashion to Reason; but his ironic style was not understood. Convinced of his error, he wanted to change his plan: "I will put a capital I on the frontispiece of my Feuille Volante, so that the public will be aware of it" (I, as in Irony), he declares at the end of the first volume. In fact, van Effen himself, a serious man, found it difficult to sustain the satirical tone. In short, La Bagatelle was not a success.
=500  \\$aPreface in the issue of Monday 5 September 1718: "to bring Men back from the ridiculous impressions of Custom and Fashion to the eternal and invariable principles of Reason, which must be the only Rule of our Conduct".
=504  \\$aevery volume contains an index
=504  \\$aEdited by James L. Schorr (ed.), ‘La Bagatelle’ (1718-1719): a critical edition of Justus van Effen’s journal, in  'Oxford University Studies in the Enlightenment', November 2014. ISBN 9780729411493, 352 pages,
=590  \\$aOù l'on prête des Sophismes ingénieux au Vice & à l'Extravagance, pour en faire mieux sentir le ridicule. Par Mr. van Effen, Docteur en Droit, & Membre de la Société Royale de Londres

=100  \\$aDrouaux, Étienne$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q28494512$98519
=245  \\$aMéthode nouvelle pour apprendre le plain-chant$bDivise en quatre parties
=250  \\$a4th ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bLangronne$c1705
=300  \\$a[viii]-144 pages$bmusical examples
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1672 Paris by Robert & Ballard
=500  \\$aÉtienne Drouaux was a musician and composer active in Paris in the last third of the 17th century.
=500  \\$aDrouaux is best known as the author of a method of plainsong which enjoyed a certain success, since about ten editions were published between 1672 and 1705. This method was part of a wave of publications of new methods which tended to give a somewhat secure basis to the practice of plainchant. But it appears that Drouaux was largely inspired by Jean Millet's method of 1666, keeping the most practical elements and eliminating the old authorities that encumbered it.
=500  \\$aDrouaux' first name is really Étienne (or Estienne), not Henri Blaise, as Fétis or Ton thought

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aMaggi, Girolamo$dc. 1523-1572$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q5564769$98540
=245  \\$aDe equuleo
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bFrisius$c1664
=300  \\$a[xxx]-196-[14] pages$bbound in white vellum, engraved title page, illustrations, 1 inserted folded page$c7x13 cm
=500  \\$aTreatise on torture devices written in 1571, first published posthumously 1609.
=500  \\$aMaggi was an Italian scholar, jurist, poet, military engineer, urban planner, philologist, archaeologist, mathematician, and naturalist who studied at Bologna under Francis Robortello. He authored several works, including a collection of poems on the Flemish wars, and several on the subject of philosophy.
=500  \\$aMaggi was a judge and military defense engineer in Famagusta on Cyprus when the island was invaded by Ottoman Turks in 1571. Besieged by the Turks, he invented machines to defend Famagusta against their attacks. When the island was conquered, Maggi was sent to the dungeons at Constantinople where, locked in chains, he wrote from memory two detailed treatises, De tintinnabulis, on bells and carillons, and the explicitly illustrated De equuleo, on torture devices.In attempts to be freed, he dedicated the first treatise to Carolus Rym (Charles Ramire), ambassador to the Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian II, and the second treatise to François de Noailles, bishop of Aire and ambassador to the King of France. They were pleased with his works, and endeavoured to obtain his release. Their efforts, however, were brought to light as he was being released to the Italian ambassador. The prison captain ordered him to be detained and executed by strangulation. His two treatises were published posthumously in 1608 and 1609, respectively.

=500  \\$aMaggi was an Italian scholar, jurist, poet, military engineer, urban planner, philologist, archaeologist, mathematician, and naturalist who studied at Bologna under Francis Robortello. He authored several works, including a collection of poems on the Flemish wars, and several on the subject of philosophy.

=500  \\$aMaggi was a judge and military defense engineer in Famagusta on Cyprus when the island was invaded by Ottoman Turks in 1571. Besieged by the Turks, he invented machines to defend Famagusta against their attacks. When the island was conquered, Maggi was sent to the dungeons at Constantinople where, locked in chains, he wrote from memory two detailed treatises, De tintinnabulis, on bells and carillons, and the explicitly illustrated De equuleo, on torture devices.In attempts to be freed, he dedicated the first treatise to Carolus Rym (Charles Ramire), ambassador to the Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian II, and the second treatise to François de Noailles, bishop of Aire and ambassador to the King of France. They were pleased with his works, and endeavoured to obtain his release. Their efforts, however, were brought to light as he was being released to the Italian ambassador. The prison captain ordered him to be detained and executed by strangulation. His two treatises were published posthumously in 1608 and 1609, respectively.

=041  \\$ager$hdan
=100  \\$aHolberg, Ludvig$d1684-1754$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q216692$98546
=245  \\$aPeter Paars$bein comisches Heldengedicht
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bMumme$c1750
=300  \\$a[lxviii]-420 pages$b14 inserted engraved plates, engraved title pages and frontispiece
=500  \\$aTitle page has emblem "In Spe et Labore"
=500  \\$aPeder Paars is a comic-epic poem that appeared in four parts in the years 1719-20 under the pseudonym of Hans Michelsen. The poem is a parody of the heroic epics of antiquity and Renaissance. Holberg particularly alludes to Vergil's great Roman epic Aeneid.
=500  \\$aThe poem enjoyed great success, but the description of conditions on Anholt prompted the then owner, Frederik Rostgaard, to complain to the king, demanding that the book be burned by the executioner. The king nevertheless decided that the writing - although it "could rather have been omitted than written" - could be accepted, as it was a "fictitious sketch." 
=500  \\$aHolberg was a writer, essayist, philosopher, historian and playwright born in Bergen, Norway, during the time of the Dano-Norwegian dual monarchy. He was influenced by Humanism, the Enlightenment and the Baroque. Holberg is considered the founder of modern Danish and Norwegian literature. He is best known for the comedies he wrote in 1722–1723 for the Lille Grønnegade Theatre in Copenhagen.
=500  \\$aPaars was a breakthrough in Holberg's writing in the direction of satire and the many comedies for which he is still known.
=500  \\$aThe composer J.A. Scheibe translated Peder Paars into German. In 1740 he became kapellmeister at the court of the danisch king Christian IV, and remained in Denmark until his death. He had a very sharp pen, evident in his satirical writings or political pamphlets,  but also in the first biography of his friend Baron Ludvig Holberg, The biography not only provides information on Holberg but also indirectly on Scheibe.
=504  \\$aPaars and his crew discover that the inhabitants of Anholt, who "live Christianly and feed on debris", are plundering and robbing the castaways. The rest of the island is watching the commoners who live in the blackest superstition. The bailiff passes judgement in his own favour, while the priest relies on old Catholic sermons.

https://www.hf.uio.no/imv/english/research/projects/power/projectdescription/holberg/

=500  \\$aJoseph Addison was an English essayist, poet, playwright and politician. His name is usually remembered alongside that of his long-standing friend Richard Steele, with whom he founded The Spectator magazine. His simple prose style marked the end of the mannerisms and conventional classical images of the 17th century.[
=500  \\$aThe Gallica-digitalisation in the version revised by the actor Jean Claude Gilles Colson (1725-1778) dit Bellecour, was according to Léris first performed in 1762:
https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k9738993k.texteImage
=500  \\$a First edition of the French translation by Destouches. 
=520  \\$aLady Truman is apparently widowed when she receives word that her husband Sir George has been killed in battle during the recent war. As she is now the wealthy owner of an estate she is pursued by two suitors, but concerningly the house is disturbed at night by repeated sounds of ghostly drumming. After the drumming has scared off the two suitors Mr. Tinsel and Mr. Fantome it is revealed to be the work of Sir George, still very much alive.

=500  \\$aJohann Joseph Kausch was a Silesian physician and writer. He not only wrote various writings and treatises in the field of medicine, but also published writings on aesthetics, poetry and politics. In Trachenberg, as personal physician at the court of Prince Franz Philipp Adrian Hatzfeld (1717-1779), he began to study psychology through the study of French philosophers.

=041  \\$alat$hlat
=245  \\$aMonita secreta of de geheime instructiën die door de Jesuieten in stilte worden nageleefd
=260  \\$aOostburg$bBronswijk$c1868
=300  \\$a56 pages
=500  \\$aAnti-Jesuit pamphlet
=500  \\$aThe Monita secreta ("Secret Instructions") is an anonymous document from 1614 whose original title is Monita privata Societatis Iesu . This booklet gives instructions to the Jesuits on how to proceed in order to gain power and wealth. It is a fake - and known as such since 1615 - but it had great success with the enemies of the Jesuits, including the 19th and 20th centuries.  Scholars regard the document as an anti-Jesuit forgery, written by Hieronymus Zahorowski, a Jesuit dismissed from the Order.
=520  \\$aAccording to the Monita, Jesuits are to use every means at their disposal to acquire wealth for the order. For instance, Jesuits are encouraged to entice promising young men to enter the order and endow it with their estates; rich widows are to be cajoled and dissuaded from remarriage. Every means is to be used for the advancement of Jesuits to bishoprics or other ecclesiastical dignities and to discredit the members of other orders, while the world is to be persuaded that the Society is animated by the purest and least interested motives: the reputation of those who quit it is to be assailed and maligned in every way.

=245  \\$aLes Psaumes de David, mis en vers françois, & les cantiques sacrés
=250  \\$aRev. ed.
=260  \\$aBasel$bImhof$c1774
=300  \\$a472-180 pages$bgilded edges
=500  \\$aIncluding one loose page with ms. notes about psalmbooks, probably written by D.W.L. Milo, on the backside of a concert flyer.
=500  \\$aThe translation of the psalms go back to John Calvin (1509-1564). In 1562 a collection of psalms (known as the Genevan Psalms) was published, suitable to be sung during the service. Calvin had started rhyming in Strasbourg himself. Back in Geneva, he handed this work over to Clément Marot and Beza, while he asked Guillaume Franc, Louis Bourgeois and Maitre Pierre to compose the music. Calvin's zeal in making a collection of psalms arose from his wish to use the Bible alone, also for the hymn. Later editions were edited by members of the 'Compagnie des pasteurs de l'église protestante de Genève'.

=100  \\$aDorat, Claude-Joseph$d1734-1780$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q361456$98577
=245  \\$aLes Prôneurs, ou Le Tartuffe littéraire,$bComédie en trois actes, en vers.
=260  \\$aParis$bDelalain$c1777
=300  \\$aviii-87 pages$b4 insterted engravings
=500  \\$aA lively satire of the people in Julie de Lespinasse's society, i.e. the philosophical party. Dorat kept it in his portfolio for several years without being able to have it performed. The philosophers, who were not spared, used the powerful men of their party to prevent the play from being performed. The main character of the play is D'Alembert who, under the name of "Callidès", plays the role of leader of the advocates. The scene in which he initiates a young follower into the mysteries of the order is very pleasant. In this play we find some portraits drawn with a rather vigorous brush, among others, those of Palissot and Clément de Dijon, of whom Dorat had reason to complain; of the former, because he had portrayed him in a less than advantageous manner in his Dunciade; of the latter, because he had made a bitter criticism of his poem De la déclamation.
=500  \\$amotto by Voltaire on the frontispiece: "Le Philosophe est seul, & l'Imposteur fait Secte."

=500  \\$aBenjamin Hederich (1675-1748) was a German encyclopedia and textbook author. From 1702 he worked as a teacher, first at the school in Kloster Berge, later as rector in Grossenhain. In his spare time he wrote introductions to numerous sciences, as well as dictionaries and textbooks in Greek and Latin. His guidance on the noblest historical sciences includes the fields of chronology, genealogy, heraldry, numismatics and diplomacy; without using this term, he put together a canon of auxiliary sciences that has survived almost unchanged to this day.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in  1717
=561  \\$aEx libris Walther Graefe (stamp)
=590  \\$aworinne Nicht allein von den Ländern, Städten, Schlössern, Meeren, Seen, Flüssen, Brunnen u.d.g. wie Auch von den Zeiten, Völckern, Geschlechten, Personen, alten Gebräuchen und Seltenheiten, Göttern, Göttinnen und anderen zur Geographie, Chronologie, Genealogie, Historie, Notitia Auctorum, den antiqvitäten und der Mythologie gehörigen merckwürdigkeiten, derer in den griechischen und lateinische auf Schulen üblichen Auctoribus classicis Meldung geschiehet, eine Nöthige Nachricht gegeben sondern auch was von Technicis aus der Grammatica, Rhetoria, Logica and Poetica der Studirenden Jugend insonderheit zu wissen dienlich, mit seinen Definitionibus und Exempeln zulänglich erläutert Wird

=100  \\$aVolkmann, Johann Jacob$d1732-1803$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q113563$98583
=245  \\$aHistorisch-kritische Nachrichten von Italien $p1-3/3
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bFritsch$c1770-1
=300  \\$a3 vols. (xxvi-682-[8] + viii-872 + [viii]-846-[42] pages)$bengraved frontispiece, red edges, engraved title vignet
=500  \\$aOne of the most influential German art books of the 18th century. Spread over three volumes, it systematically provides information about churches, palaces, art collections, musical life, but also about the history of all important Italian cities from Turin to Naples. As a guide to historical Italy, the 'Volkmann' accompanied Goethe, Karl Philipp Moritz, Johann Gottfried Seume and many other Germans on their travels. Goethe, for example, wrote to Charlotte von Stein in 1787: " I am now reading the good, dry Volckmanns zweyten Theil to note what I have not yet seen." (Kippenberg)
=500  \\$a3 identical engraved title vignets depicting 2 little boys holding a map of Italy
=500  \\$aFrontispiece engraving by Christian Gottlieb Geyser (1742-1803)
=500  \\$amanuscript notes on front matter of vol. 1 and 2
=500  \\$apensil markings throughout
=561  \\$aEx libris Riegel- und Wiesnersche Lesebibliothek Nürnberg (plate)
=590  \\$awelche eine Beschreibung dieses Landes, der Sitten und Gebraüche, der Regierungsform, Handlung, Oekonomie, des Zustandes der Wissenschaften und insonderheit der Werke der Kunst nebst einer Beurtheilung derselben enthalten. Aus den neuesten französischen und englischen Reisebeschreibungen und aus eignen Anmerkungen zusammengetragen.

=500  \\$aJohan Georg Hamann was a German librettist and writer, a cousin of his famous nephew of the same name J. G. Hamann (1730-1788). He became a private tutor and was active as a publicist, contributing to Gottsched's periodical 'Die vernünftigen Tadlerinnen'.

=245  \\$aAdres-Calender der Königl. Preußl. Haupt- und Residentz-Städte Berlin

=500  \\$aadress book of Berlin in 1764
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars appeared annually between 1704 and 1918 under different titles.
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars list the higher-ranking persons and office holders of the royal Prussian residential cities of Berlin and Potsdam as well as their authorities, administrations and organizations. The address and description of the authorities are listed, as well as the person's name, official title and private address. At the end of each entry is an index of names. From 1878 onwards, information from the neighboring city of Charlottenburg is also included.

=100  \\$aChoffin, David Étienne$d1703-1773$4aut$98590
=245  \\$aAmusemens philologiques en prose et en vers$bou mélange agréable de diverses pièces, concernant l'histoire des personnes célèbres, les évènemens mémorables & l'histoire naturelle$p3
=260  \\$aHalle$bMaison des Orphelins$c1780
=300  \\$a[xxx]-397 pages$bengraved frontispiece, title page in red and black ink, title page engraved with editor's emblem
=500  \\$aLater edition
=500  \\$aoriginal in 2 vols. , 1749-1750
=500  \\$aChoffin was a scholar and philologist, born in Héricourt (F) on October 2, 1703, died in Halle (D) in January 1773.  He obtained the double position of professor of modern languages at the school of the Orphans and at the university of Halle, and he contributed by his writings and his lessons to spread the use of French in Saxony.
=500  \\$aEditor's emblem depicting sunbeams & cultivated land with saying "illo splendete levabor' and the initials WH, referring to Weisenhaus Halle  (La Maison des Orphelins à Halle). The Latin motto "Illo splendente levabor" (By his splendor I will be exalted) was intended to testify to the godliness of the institution. The sower in the foreground was interpreted by Bible-loving contemporaries as a reference to the Gospel of Mark (4:14): "The sower sows the word." And this was precisely Francke's basic concern: to change the world by means of the word.
=500  \\$aIntresting frontispiece engraving, depicting Germany, rulers' portraits and battlefields, with inscription "Teutschland hofft der Friedens Zeit - L'Allemagne attend le tems de la paix".
=501  \\$aBound in with ‘Dictionnaire abrégé de la fable ou de la mythologie’

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aGodeau, Antoine$d1605-1672$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q586272$97907
=245  \\$aPoësies chrestiennes
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bPetit$c1660
=300  \\$a508 pages$bengraved title page
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau was a French bishop, poet and exegete.
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau (1605-1672) first published the Poësies Chrestiennes in 1633 in the context of the Catholic Reformation which encouraged spiritual revival. This lyric collection is emblematic of his comprehensive poetic and spiritual work. Godeau became the Bishop of Grasse in 1636 and devoted his poetic gifts to enlightening the readers. This new edition is the latest version of the Poësies Chrestiennes (1660), which is pastoral Catholic verse addressed to the socialites of the time. The versatile poet expressed himself in various forms, registers and topics to convey the Christian dogma and the Bible. The content and the purpose of the book fluctuated. The Poësies chrestiennes was thus a field for experimentation : it became Antoine Godeau's laboratory for all his pastoral and lyric work. The poet defined the principles of a poetry which was based on the conciliation of divine enthusiasm and reason, a poetry where grace and beauty met. The paraphrase of the Scriptures was an opportunity to explore the conciliation of Parnassus and Calvary, as well as the specificity of a classical poetic language in the making, endowing it with gentleness and clarity. Poetry appeared to be the ideal way to instill Christian truths in the heart of the faithful. The religious conversion of secular literary rhetoric prepared the layman to hear the poet-preacher’s vigorous speech. Antoine Godeau tempered his Augustinian anthropology by promoting a life both wordly and pious, in chime with the ideal of Christian “honnêteté”. The poet spiritualized profane aesthetics, which showed his unrelenting desire to adapt his conversion discourse to a public eager to be edified by the “delectare”.
=504  \\$aCamille Venner, Édition critique des "Poësies chrestiennes" (1660) d'Antoine Godeau précédée d'une introduction sur la pastorale lyrique et catholique de cet auteur, These, Université de Lorraine, 2018
https://hal.univ-lorraine.fr/tel-01752385

=100  \\$aSaavedra Fajardo, Diego de$d1584-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2715411$98592
=245  \\$aIdea de un principe politico christiano, representada en cien empresas
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bJanssonius$c1664
=300  \\$a[xxxv]-983 pages
=500  \\$aDiego de Saavedra Fajardo (1584-1648) was a Spanish diplomat and man of letters.

=500  \\$ain 1640 Saavedra published the anti-Machiavellian emblem book Empresas Políticas. Idea de un príncipe político cristiano, a hundred short essays about the education of a prince. This work was written primarily for the son of King Philip IV. It passed through a number of editions and was translated in several languages.
=500  \\$aSaavedra's 'Idea de un príncipe político cristiano' was a very erudite work that uses the literary sort of emblem, put by Andrea Alciato with his 'Emblemata' translated in 1549 and that has a mainly moral and philosophical character. His work, however, was mainly inspired by the 'Emblemata política' (1618), by Jakob Bruck Angermunt, being the intention of the author to compose a guide for the suitable political formation of a Christian prince. 
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1640

=041  \\$alat$afre
=245  \\$aCantus diversi pro Dominicis, festis et feriis per annum
=260  \\$aToulouse$bDouladoure$c1745
=300  \\$a286 pages
=500  \\$apages 282-286 include a 'Manière pour bien chanter dans un chœur' (without title page), derived from 'Trois methodes faciles pour apprendre le plein-chant' (1689).
=500  \\$aThis set of three anonymous methods could have been commissioned by Claude Bachelu, a bookseller from Lyon who was worried on several occasions for counterfeiting or for having distributed banned books. Having published numerous works of spirituality and theology, Bachelu brought out in his name a collection of Cantus diversi (1689). Like Parisian colleagues such as La Caille, he doubled this publication with a theoretical counterpart, thus the 'Trois methodes'. Modeled from the easy method designed for the Parisian seminary of Saint-Nicolas du Chardonnet, they then benefited from a long editorial existence since they are found at the end of several other books imitating that of Bachelu, and this until the middle of the 18th century. The 'Three methods' are (partly) included with a new title page and new compositions in the Cantus diversi by Claude Moulu (Lyon, 1700) and by Gaspard Henault (Toulouse, 1745) or, without title page, in the Cantus diversi ex Graduali Romano by Pierre Valfray (Lyon, 1724) and this edition by Joseph Douladure (Toulouse, 1745). (for more information see: https://www.cantus-scholarum.univ-tours.fr/ressources/sources/methodes-faciles-de-plain-chant/trois-methodes-1698/)
=500  \\$ams. scribblings on back matter

=500  \\$aMoritz von Strachwitz (1822-1847) was a German lyric poet. When traveling in Italy in 1847 he was taken ill in Venice, and died in Vienna. Although he had thus only reached his twenty-fifth year, he revealed a lyric genius of remarkable force and originality. His early death was a great loss to German letters; for he was by far the most promising of the younger lyric poets of his time.

=500  \\$aA picaresque novel, in the style of Le Sage’s Gil Blas. Thibault was governor of Talmont, and this is his only known work. Set in Spain, it deals with the love story of a rogue, facing the galleys. It was enormously popular, being translated into English, German, Iberian, and Castillian. Also published under the title: Histoire comique et galante de Pédrille del Campo.

=100  \\$aBlumauer, Aloys$d1755-1798$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q79087$98614
=245  \\$aVirgil's Aeneis in neun Gesängen
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bKöhler$c1841
=300  \\$a296 pages$b36 plates inserted
=500  \\$aAloys Blumauer, also known as Alois Blumauer or Johannes Aloysius Blumauer, (1755-1798) was an Austrian poet.
His works, which are chiefly coarse satires on the clergy and on the Jesuits (of which he himself had become a member a year before its dissolution in 1773), enjoyed a wide popularity. He is remembered, however, chiefly for his Abenteuer des frommen Helden Æneas (1784–88; published with introduction and commentary by E. Griesbach, 1872), a coarse travesty on Vergil's Aeneid. Blumauer is also remembered as an acquaintance of Mozart, the lyrics of whose Lied der Freiheit (KV 506, 1786) he penned.

=245  \\$aHistoire des Sevarambes
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bRoger$c1702

=500  \\$a2 volumes in 1
=500  \\$aThe History of Sevarambians is a utopian novel by Denis Vairasse published in 1675 as The History of the Sevarites or Sevarambi. Originally published in English, it was quickly translated into French and expanded, with parts two and three appearing in 1677 as L’Histoire des Sévarambes. Two further instalments were published in French in 1679. The novel did not appear in its completed form in English until 1738. The novel depicts an ideal world in Australia.

=500  \\$aChristian devotional literature
=500  \\$aThe term "Erbauungsliteratur' (edification literature), first mentioned around the 14th century, originally describes popular writings with a religious motivation. Edification literature is not theological literature, as it does not pursue scientific discourses and has no dogmatic intentions. Rather, with the changes of the modern era, there was a focus on inwardness, which stood out through increased piety. It was a guide to a virtuous life that was intended to emotionally edify the mind. 
=500  \\$aJohannes Lassenius (1636-1692) was a German Lutheran theologian and devotional writer of the Baroque period.

=500  \\$aWilhelmus Schortinghuis (1700-1750) was a Dutch Reformed clergyman. He is best known for his book 'Het Inninge Christendom' (1740) and the "vijf nieten" (the five nots): "ik wil niet, ik kan niet, ik weet niet, ik heb niet en ik deug niet" (I don't want to, I can't, I don't know, I don't have and I'm no good), with which he wanted to make clear. that a man could contribute nothing to his salvation. He is regarded as a representative of the late phase of the 'Nadere Reformatie', which is often referred to as Reformed Pietism.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aSenault, Jean-François$d1599-1672$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3165889$98453
=245  \\$aDe l'usage des passions
=260  \\$aParis$bJournel$c1660
=300  \\$alxxii-492 pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1641
=500  \\$aA book on the ‘usage’ of emotions by the French Augustinian preacher, Jean-François Senault. He approached the subject of the ‘passions’ from a variety of angles: their uses and dangers, how to moderate them and how a prince should use them. The treatise was often reprinted in different formats and translated into English, German, Italian and Spanish. The work is divided into two parts, the first of which deals with the passions in general and the last with each in particular.
=500  \\$aOf the nature of passions -- Of the disorder of passions -- Of the government of passions -- Of the commerce of passions with vertue and vice -- Of the power that passions have upon the will of man -- Of love and hatred -- Of desire and eschewing -- Of hope and despair -- Of audacity and fear -- Of choler or anger -- Of delight and sorrow.

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aFleming, Paul$d1609-1640$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q77418$98650
=245  \\$aGeist- und Weltliche Poëmata
=260  \\$aJena$bSengenwalden$c1660
=300  \\$a[xii]-676-[27] pages
=500  \\$aPaul Fleming (1609-1640), was a German physician and poet. Fleming is one of the writers now called "the Silesian poets" or "the Silesian school". As a lyricist he stands in the front rank of German poets.
=500  \\$aFleming wrote the hymn in nine stanzas "In allen meinen Taten" on the melody of "Innsbruck, ich muss dich lassen" by Heinrich Isaac, which is contained in several hymnals. Johann Sebastian Bach used the final stanza to close both cantatas Meine Seufzer, meine Tränen (BWV 13) and Sie werden euch in den Bann tun (BWV 44). The complete hymn is the base for Bach's chorale cantata In allen meinen Taten (BWV 97). Already in the 17th century another composer, David Pohle (1624–1695), had set twelve of Fleming's love-songs to music. Johannes Brahms set "Lass dich nur nichts bedauern" as Geistliches Lied, Op. 30.
=500  \\$acontains an engraved title page and a portrait of the author on the frontispiece
=534  \\$aTeutsche Poemata, published posthumously in 1642
=561  \\$aEx libris Heinrich Sieling (plate & stamp)

=100  \\$aCalvin, Jean$d1509-1564$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q37577$95913

=260  \\$aParis$aCharenton$bCellier$c1675
=300  \\$a[626]-8-[4] pages$bembossed leather cover, front- and backmatter contains manuscript notes in French and cyphers$epostcard 
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1551, the translations of 150 Psalms of David by Clement Marot (1496-1544) as completed by Theodore de Bèze (1519-1605, Calvin's successor as spiritual leader of the Republic of Geneva) were used almost exclusively by the Calvinists (Genevan Psalter). The psalter was the main medium of popular fervour among the Reformed. The Edict of Nantes forbade Reformed worship in towns where the King of France resided and the only town allowed around Paris was Charenton. 
=500  \\$aFollowed by The Form of Ecclesiastical Prayers, The Form of Administering Baptism, The Manner of Celebrating Holy Communion, The Catechism, and Daily Exercise of the Christian.

=100  \\$aDu Roullet, François Louis Gaud Lebland$cMarquis$d1716-1786$4lbt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3083494$98660
=245  \\$aIphigénie en Aulide.$bTragédie-opéra en trois actes
=260  \\$aParis$bAntoine$c1793
=300  \\$a24 pages
=500  \\$a'Iphigénie en Aulide'  is an opera in three acts by Christoph Willibald Gluck, the first work he wrote for the Paris stage. The libretto was based on Jean Racine's tragedy Iphigénie, itself based on the play Iphigenia in Aulis by Euripides. The choreography was by Gaétan Vestris. It was premiered on 19 April 1774 by the Paris Opéra in the second Salle du Palais-Royal and revived in a slightly revised version the following year.

=245  \\$aRembrandt van Rijn$b[Algemeen Handelsblad, 1852]
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bDrukkerij van het Algemeen Handelsblad$c1852
=300  \\$a6 pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aNewspaper extract of the Algemeen Handelsblad of 28 mai 1852 (an influential Amsterdam-based liberal daily newspaper published between 1828 and 1970), on the occasion of King Willem III unveiling in 1852 a cast-iron Rembrandt monument designed by Louis Royer on the Amsterdam Botermarkt-square (named Rembrandtplein since 1876). 
=500  \\$a4 pages Biography, ending with poem by Thijm, plus 2 pages text that appeared on the title page of the Newspaper.
=500  \\$aThe biography ends with a long celebrating poem on Rembrandt by J.A. Alberdingk Thijm (1820-1889) titled "Een Harptoon in het Akkoord der Rembrandtshulde"
https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/albe003voor01_01/albe003voor01_01_0016.php
=501  \\$a1    1698    Haegse Mercur, nos. 31 & 32 (19 & 22 November 1698)
2    1720    Amsterdamse Donderdaegse Courant Anno 1720 no. 71

=041  \\$ager
=245  \\$aUnter Allerhöchster Autoriteit Ihro Kön. Maj. zu Dännemark, Norwegen u. Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen 40stes Stück. Montag den 7ten October 1799
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1799
=300  \\$a4 pages$bquadruple-folded pages$c42x36c cm
=500  \\$aThe Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen (SchlHA) is the justice journal of the German federal state of Schleswig-Holstein and at the same time one of the oldest periodicals of the state.
The Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen date back to the time of the duchies of Schleswig and Holstein and have been published since 1750.[1] They are an announcement journal that was published under the same title by both the kings of Denmark and the diverse rulers in Schleswig-Holstein such as the House of Schleswig-Holstein-Gottorf. Today, the publisher is the state's Ministry of Justice, which has left the editorship to the Higher Regional Court of Schleswig. They are divided into a monthly Part A (with the editorial content of a legal journal and contributions on case law in the judicial district of the state's only Higher Regional Court) and a twice-monthly Part B (advertising section and judicial notices). It is therefore an official journal and not an advertising journal.
Part B of the Schleswig-Holstein Advertisements was published twice a month (on the 15th and 30th of a month) in printed form as a justice gazette until the end of 2014. The publication of a written edition of Part B has been dispensed with since 1 January 2015. Therefore, from this date onwards, all issues of Part B (which in future will only be published once on the 30th of a month) will only be made available digitally and free of charge.

=260  \\$aBaden-Baden$bBaldinger$c1771
=300  \\$a220 pages$bbound in cardboard, leather spine, marbled front- and backcover, music examples
=500  \\$aSaint Leodegar (c. 616-678) was abbot of the Saint-Maixent, counselor to Queen Bathildis, martyred Burgundian Bishop of Autun, and supporter of King Childerik IILeodegar of Poitiers . Leodegar was an opponent of Ebroin, the Frankish Mayor of the Palace of Neustria, and the leader of the faction of Burgundian nobles. His torture and death made him a martyr and saint.
=500  \\$atitle: A bundle of psalms and hymns, which are both for Vespers and for the Hours of the Day: according to the rite of the Roman breviary, dedicated to the ingenuous youth of the ancient school of the divine Leodegarius of Lucerne. To which are added the Marian antiphons, eight tones to the Magnificat, various litanies, etc., published by order of the Superiors

=100  \\$aFélice, Fortunato Bartolomeo de$d1723-1789$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3078548$98919
=245  \\$aRemarques sur la structure des orgues tirées de l'Encyclopédie d'Yverdon
=260  \\$aYverdon$bs.n.$c1825
=300  \\$a197 pages$bindex, illustrations, charts, 1 fold-out sheet
=500  \\$aThe 'Encyclopédie ou Dictionnaire universel raisonné des connaissances humaines', ed. by Fortunato Bartolomeo De Felice, appeared between 1770 and 1780 in Yverdon; it was strongly anti-religious.
=500  \\$aDe Felice, an Italian nobleman, was a famed author, philosopher, scientist, and is said to have been one of the most important publishers of the 18th century. He is considered a pioneer of education in Switzerland, and a formative contributor to the European Enlightenment.
=500  \\$aIn an accompanying letter from Mr. Boogaarts to Ton Koopman, it is suggested that the copy of the Yverdon article from 1770 was made by Frans C. Smit (1800-1876) around c. 1825, and that this manuscript was part of the inheritance of Arie Bouman (Dutch barritone and organist 1911-1999), whose personal archives are preserved in the Utrecht Organ Archive iof the Utrecht University Library. As an organ consultant, Bouman left his mark on the Dutch organ scene for decades.

=500  \\$aEssay about the book and the editions by Robert Fruin (1903): https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/frui001vers08_01/frui001vers08_01_0030.php. The publishers name, Jan Heindrikze, could be a pseudonym for Josua Van Der Straten, whose 1669 edition didn't sell as much because of another, more elaborate one in 1670 by Johannes Naeranus. 
Naeranus commented heavily on Van der Stratens edition; the Heindrikze edition also contains this commentary. 
This theory presents this edition as an attempt of Van der Straten to recycle a part of his earlier print.
